%% Diff
\usepackage{xcolor}
% Define commands for highlighting
% diff
\usepackage[most]{tcolorbox} % for boxes with transparency
% Define colors with transparency (opacity value)
\definecolor{GreenBG}{rgb}{0,1,0}
\definecolor{RedBG}{rgb}{1,0,0}
% Define tcolorbox environments for highlighting
\newtcbox{\greenhighlight}[1][]{%
  on line,
  colframe=GreenBG,
  colback=GreenBG!50!white, % 50% transparent green
  boxrule=0pt,
  arc=0pt,
  boxsep=0pt,
  left=1pt,
  right=1pt,
  top=2pt,
  bottom=2pt,
  tcbox raise base
}
\newtcbox{\redhighlight}[1][]{%
  on line,
  colframe=RedBG,
  colback=RedBG!50!white, % 50% transparent red
  boxrule=0pt,
  arc=0pt,
  boxsep=0pt,
  left=1pt,
  right=1pt,
  top=2pt,
  bottom=2pt,
  tcbox raise base
}

\begin{document}


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Frontmatter
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\begin{frontmatter}
\begin{highlights}
\pdfbookmark[1]{Highlights}{highlights}

\item Neural trajectories in the hippocampus exhibited greater variability during a working memory (WM) task compared to those in the entorhinal cortex and amygdala regions.

\item The distance of neural trajectories between encoding and retrieval states in the hippocampus was memory-load dependent during a WM task.


\item Hippocampal neural trajectories fluctuated between the encoding and retrieval states in a task-dependent manner during both baseline and sharp-wave ripple (SWR) periods.

\item Hippocampal neural trajectories shifted from encoding to retrieval states during SWR period.

\end{highlights}\title{
Hippocampal neural fluctuations between memory encoding and retrieval states during a working memory task in humans: Encoding-to-retrieval shift during sharp-wave ripples
}\author[1]{Yusuke Watanabe\corref{cor1}}
\author[2,3,4]{Yuji Ikegaya}
\author[1,5]{Takufumi Yanagisawa}

\address[1]{Institute for Advanced Cocreation studies, Osaka University, 2-2 Yamadaoka, Suita, 565-0871, Osaka, Japan}
\address[2]{Graduate School of Pharmaceutical Sciences, The University of Tokyo, 7-3-1 Hongo, Tokyo, 113-0033, Japan}
\address[3]{Institute for AI and Beyond, The University of Tokyo, 7-3-1 Hongo, Tokyo, 113-0033, Japan}
\address[4]{Center for Information and Neural Networks, National Institute of Information and Communications Technology, 1-4 Yamadaoka, Suita City, 565-0871, Osaka, Japan}
\address[5]{Department of Neurosurgery, Osaka University Graduate School of Medicine, 2-2 Yamadaoka, Osaka, 565-0871, Japan}

\cortext[cor1]{Corresponding author. Tel: +81-6-6879-3652}%%Graphical abstract

%DIF < % Introduction

\section{Introduction}
Working memory (WM) plays a \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{crucial role in everyday life, yet its underlying neural mechanisms remain to be fully elucidated}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{critical role in our daily activities, but the neural mechanisms underlying it are not completely understood}\DIFaddend . Particularly, the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{function of the }\DIFdelend hippocampus, a \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{vital brain region contributing to memory, commands }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{key brain region involved in memory, warrants }\DIFaddend ongoing investigation \cite{scoville_loss_1957,squire_legacy_2009,boran_persistent_2019,kaminski_persistently_2017,kornblith_persistent_2017,faraut_dataset_2018,borders_hippocampus_2022,li_functional_2023,dimakopoulos_information_2022}. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Gaining insight into the role }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Enhancing our understanding }\DIFaddend of the hippocampus\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{'s role }\DIFaddend in working memory \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{fosters a deeper understanding of cognitive processesand facilitates }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{can lead to deeper insights into cognitive processes, thereby promoting }\DIFaddend the development of cognitive training strategies and interventions. 
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin 

\DIFaddend \indent
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Transient and synchronous oscillations, referred to as sharp }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Sharp }\DIFaddend wave ripples (SWR), \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{are known to be associated with various }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{transient and synchronous oscillations generated by the hippocampus, are associated with key }\DIFaddend cognitive functions, including memory replay \cite{wilson_reactivation_1994,nadasdy_replay_1999,lee_memory_2002,davidson_hippocampal_2009}, memory consolidation \cite{girardeau_selective_2009,ego-stengel_disruption_2010,fernandez-ruiz_long-duration_2019,kim_corticalhippocampal_2022}, memory recall \cite{wu_hippocampal_2017,norman_hippocampal_2019,norman_hippocampal_2021}, and neural plasticity \cite{behrens_induction_2005,norimoto_hippocampal_2018}. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Therefore, SWR might constitute a fundamental aspect of processing in the hippocampus and contribute to }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Consequently, SWRs could be critical to hippocampal processing and influence }\DIFaddend working memory performance. However, studies \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{investigating the effects }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{examining the influence }\DIFaddend of SWRs on working memory \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{remain scarce \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{jadhav_awake_2012} }\hspace{0pt}%DIFAUXCMD
, and are predominantly limited to rodent models using navigation tasks, in which the exact timings of memory acquisition and recall are not distinguished.
}%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{are scarce \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{jadhav_awake_2012} }\hspace{0pt}%DIFAUXCMD
and primarily center on rodent models utilizing navigation tasks. Such research has not clearly differentiated between the specific timing of memory recall and acquisition.
}

\DIFaddend \indent
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Further}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Moreover}\DIFaddend , it has been \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{discovered }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{found }\DIFaddend that hippocampal neurons \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{exhibit }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{present }\DIFaddend low-dimensional representations during WM tasks. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{For instance, the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The }\DIFaddend firing patterns of place cells \cite{okeefe_hippocampus_1971,okeefe_place_1976,ekstrom_cellular_2003,kjelstrup_finite_2008,harvey_intracellular_2009,royer_control_2012} in the hippocampus\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{are embedded within }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, for instance, align with }\DIFaddend a dynamic, nonlinear three-dimensional hyperbolic geometry in rodents \cite{zhang_hippocampal_2022}. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Moreover}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Similarly}\DIFaddend , grid cells in the entorhinal cortex (EC)\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{--- the primary gateway }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{—the main entry point }\DIFaddend to the hippocampus \cite{naber_reciprocal_2001,van_strien_anatomy_2009,strange_functional_2014}\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{--- displayed }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{—display a }\DIFaddend toroidal topology during exploration \cite{gardner_toroidal_2022}. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Nevertheless, these experiments are again constrained }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{However, these studies primarily relate }\DIFaddend to spatial navigation tasks in rodents \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, limited in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{and provide limited }\DIFaddend temporal resolution for WM tasks. Additionally, it \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{has yet to be investigated whether these findings can be generalized to humans and }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is still uncertain whether these results apply to humans or to }\DIFaddend tasks beyond navigation.
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin 

\DIFaddend \indent
In light of these considerations, this study \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{explores }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{tests }\DIFaddend the hypothesis that hippocampal neurons \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{exhibit distinct representations in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{demonstrate distinct }\DIFaddend low-dimensional \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{spaces as a 'neural trajectory'}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{representations, or 'neural trajectories', }\DIFaddend during WM tasks, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{with a particular emphasis on }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{specifically during }\DIFaddend SWR periods. To \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{test thishypothesis, we utilized }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{investigate this, we used }\DIFaddend a dataset of patients performing an eight-second Sternberg task (with high temporal resolution: 1 s for fixation, 2 s for encoding, 3 s for maintenance, and 2 s for retrieval) while their intracranial electroencephalography signals (iEEG) in the medial temporal lobe (MTL) were \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{being }\DIFdelend recorded \cite{boran_dataset_2020}. We \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{employed }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{implemented }\DIFaddend Gaussian-process factor analysis (GPFA) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{based on multiunit activities }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{on multichannel unit activity }\DIFaddend to explore low-dimensional neural trajectories, a \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{known tool for analyzing }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{proven method to analyze }\DIFaddend neural population dynamics \cite{yu_gaussian-process_2009}.
\label{sec:introduction}```tex
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
%% Methods
%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%
\section{Methods}
\subsection{Dataset}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We utilized a }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{A }\DIFaddend publicly accessible dataset \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{boran_dataset_2020} }\hspace{0pt}%DIFAUXCMD
wherein }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{was utilized \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{boran_dataset_2020}}\hspace{0pt}%DIFAUXCMD
, which included }\DIFaddend nine epilepsy patients \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{performed }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{performing }\DIFaddend a modified Sternberg task comprising the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{following }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{subsequent }\DIFaddend four phases: fixation (1 s), encoding (2 s), maintenance (3 s), and retrieval (2 s) \cite{boran_dataset_2020}. During the encoding phase, participants were \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{presented with }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{shown }\DIFaddend sets of four, six, or eight alphabetical letters, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{which we refer to }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{denoted herein }\DIFaddend as the set size. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Subsequently, participants ' task was to determine }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{During the retrieval phase, participants were required to ascertain }\DIFaddend whether a probe letter \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{presented during the retrieval phase }\DIFdelend had been previously \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{displayed }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{shown }\DIFaddend (the correct choice for the Match IN task) or not (the correct choice for the Mismatch OUT task). Intracranial EEG (iEEG) signals were \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{captured }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{collected }\DIFaddend using depth electrodes implanted within the medial temporal lobe (MTL) regions: \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the }\DIFdelend left and right hippocampal head (AHL and AHR), \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{hippocampal }\DIFdelend body (PHL and PHR), entorhinal cortex (ECL and ECR), and amygdala (AL and AR). These signals were recorded at a sampling rate of 32 kHz and within \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{a }\DIFaddend frequency range of 0.5--5,000 Hz (Figure~\ref{fig:01}A and Table~\ref{tab:01}). The iEEG signals were then resampled at a rate of 2 kHz. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We uncovered correlations between the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Correlations between }\DIFaddend experimental variables such as set size and accuracy rate \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were uncovered }\DIFaddend (Figure~\ref{fig:s01}S1). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The times }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Times }\DIFaddend of multiunit spikes were estimated using a spike sorting algorithm \cite{niediek_reliable_2016} from the Combinato package (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{(}\DIFdelend \url{https://github.com/jniediek/combinato})(Figure~\ref{fig:01}C).

\subsection{Calculation of neural trajectories using GPFA}
To \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{derive }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{extract }\DIFaddend the neural trajectories (referred to as factors; Figure~\ref{fig:01}D) within the hippocampus, entorhinal cortex (EC), and amygdala, we \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{used }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{employed }\DIFaddend GPFA \cite{yu_gaussian-process_2009} on multiunit activity data for each session (Figure~\ref{fig:01}D). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We implemented GPFA }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{GPFA was implemented }\DIFaddend using the elephant package (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{(}\DIFdelend \url{https://elephant.readthedocs.io/en/latest/reference/gpfa.html}). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We configured the bin size }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The bin size was configured }\DIFaddend as 50 ms, with no overlaps. Each factor was z-normalized across all sessions. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We calculated the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The }\DIFaddend Euclidean distance from the origin ($O$) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{using }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{was calculated based on }\DIFaddend these trajectories (Figure~\ref{fig:01}E).
\\
\indent
Within each trajectory for a region such as AHL, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we calculated }\DIFdelend the \textit{geometric medians} (i.e., $\mathrm{g_{F}}$ for fixation, $\mathrm{g_{E}}$ for encoding, $\mathrm{g_{M}}$ for maintenance, and $\mathrm{g_{R}}$ for retrieval phase) \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were calculated }\DIFaddend by establishing the median coordinates of the trajectory during the four phases (Figure~\ref{fig:01}D). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We defined the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The }\DIFaddend optimal dimensionality for GPFA \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{as }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{was defined to be }\DIFaddend three, as determined \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{via }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{using }\DIFaddend the elbow method \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{using }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{via }\DIFaddend log-likelihood values in a three-fold cross-validation approach (Figure~\ref{fig:02}B).

\subsection{Defining SWR candidates from hippocampal regions}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{To pinpoint potential SWR events in the hippocampus, we used a detection method consistent with the consensus in the field \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{liu_consensus_2022}}\hspace{0pt}%DIFAUXCMD
. We re-referenced }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{A detection method in line with the field consensus \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{liu_consensus_2022} }\hspace{0pt}%DIFAUXCMD
was used to identify potential SWR events in the hippocampus. The }\DIFaddend local field potential (LFP) signals from a region of interest (ROI), such as AHL, \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were re-referenced }\DIFaddend by subtracting the average signal outside the ROI (e.g., AHR, PHL, PHR, ECL, ECR, AL, AR) (see Figure~\ref{fig:01}A). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Using these }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{These }\DIFaddend re-referenced LFP signals \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we applied }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were used to apply }\DIFaddend a ripple-band filter (80--140 Hz) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{to }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{and }\DIFaddend isolate SWR-positive (SWR$^+$) candidates (see Figure~\ref{fig:01}B). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We performed SWR detection }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{SWR detection was performed }\DIFaddend using a publicly available tool (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{(}\DIFdelend \url{https://github.com/Eden-Kramer-Lab/ripple_detection}) \cite{kay_hippocampal_2016}, with \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{some }\DIFdelend modifications such as a revised bandpass range of 80--140 Hz for human applications \cite{norman_hippocampal_2019,norman_hippocampal_2021} \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{as opposed to }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{instead of }\DIFaddend the original 150--250 Hz range \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{used primarily }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{primarily used }\DIFaddend for rodents.
\\
\indent
For SWR$^+$ candidates, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we defined }\DIFdelend SWR-negative (SWR$^-$) candidates \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were defined }\DIFaddend as control events by shuffling the timestamps of SWR$^+$ candidates across all trials and subjects. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We visually inspected the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The }\DIFaddend defined SWR$^+$/SWR$^-$ candidates \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were visually inspected }\DIFaddend (see Figure~\ref{fig:01}).

\subsection{Defining SWRs from putative hippocampal CA1 regions}
We \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{narrowed down }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{confined }\DIFaddend SWR candidates within putative CA1 regions to define SWRs. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We first identified }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{First, }\DIFaddend putative CA1 regions \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were identified }\DIFaddend as follows. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We embedded }\DIFdelend SWR$^+$/SWR$^-$ candidates within the hippocampus \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were embedded }\DIFaddend into a two-dimensional space based on \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{their }\DIFdelend superimposed spike counts per unit using UMAP (uniform manifold approximation and projection) \cite{mcinnes_umap_2018} in a supervised manner (Figure~\ref{fig:04}A). The silhouette score \cite{rousseeuw_silhouettes_1987}, a \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{validation metric for }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{measure for validating }\DIFaddend clustering, was calculated from clustered samples (Table~\ref{tab:02}). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We defined hippocampal regions with }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Hippocampal regions showcasing }\DIFaddend an average silhouette score across sessions \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{greater than }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{exceeding }\DIFaddend the 75th percentile \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were defined }\DIFaddend as putative CA1 regions, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{resulting in the identification of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{which resulted in }\DIFaddend five electrode locations \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{identified }\DIFaddend from five patients (Table~\ref{tab:03}).
\\
\indent
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We defined }\DIFdelend SWR$^+$/SWR$^-$ candidates within putative CA1 regions \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were marked }\DIFaddend as SWRs, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{meaning }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{thereby }\DIFaddend they were no longer candidates. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{SWR }\DIFaddend duration and ripple band peak amplitude \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{of SWRs followed }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{followed a }\DIFaddend log-normal \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{distributions }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{distribution }\DIFaddend (Figure~\ref{fig:04}C \& E). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We visually inspected }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{As seen in Figure~\ref{fig:01}, }\DIFaddend SWR$^+$/SWR$^-$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{as shown in Figure~\ref{fig:01}. We divided each SWR period }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were visually inspected. Each SWR period was divided }\DIFaddend into pre-SWR (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{at }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{from }\DIFaddend $-800$ to $-300$ ms from SWR center), mid-SWR (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{at }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{from }\DIFaddend $-250$ to $+250$ ms), and post-SWR (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{at }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{from }\DIFaddend $+300$ to $+800$ ms) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{based on }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{according to }\DIFaddend the time from the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{SWR's center }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{center of the SWR}\DIFaddend .

\subsection{Statistical Evaluation}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We conducted the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The }\DIFaddend Brunner--Munzel and Kruskal-Wallis tests \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{were conducted }\DIFaddend using the scipy package in Python \cite{virtanen_scipy_2020}. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We performed a correlation analysis }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{A correlation analysis was performed }\DIFaddend by determining the rank of the observed correlation coefficient \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{within }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{in }\DIFaddend the set-size-shuffled surrogate dataset, using a custom Python script. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Additionally, we executed }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Moreover, }\DIFaddend a bootstrap test \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{was executed }\DIFaddend using a homemade Python script.

\label{sec:methods}

\section{Results}
\subsection{iEEG recording and neural trajectory in MTL regions during a Sternberg task}
We \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{utilized a publicly accessible }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{employed a publicly available }\DIFaddend dataset \cite{boran_dataset_2020} for \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{this }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{our }\DIFaddend analysis, which \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{consists of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{comprises }\DIFaddend LFP signals (Figure 1A) from MTL regions (Table~\ref{tab:01}1) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{obtained }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{recorded }\DIFaddend during a modified Sternberg task. SWR$^+$ candidates were \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{detected within }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{identified in }\DIFaddend all hippocampal regions \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{from }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{obtained from the }\DIFaddend LFP signals, filtered by the ripple band (80--140 Hz) (Figure 1B)\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, whereas }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{. }\DIFaddend SWR$^-$ candidates were \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{defined at identical }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{delineated at the same }\DIFaddend timestamps as SWR$^+$ candidates but \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{shuffled across separate }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{scrambled across different }\DIFaddend trials (Figure 1). The \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{dataset also encompasses the }\DIFaddend multiunit spikes (Figure 1C)\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{were also included in the dataset, identified by implementation }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, which were specified through the application }\DIFaddend of a spike sorting algorithm \cite{niediek_reliable_2016}. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Relying on }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Using }\DIFaddend the 50-ms binned multiunit activity \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{devoid of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{without }\DIFaddend overlaps, we \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{applied }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{deployed }\DIFaddend GPFA \cite{yu_gaussian-process_2009} to \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{elucidate }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{unravel }\DIFaddend the neural trajectory (or factors) of MTL regions by session and region (Figure 1D). Each factor was z-normalized by session and region (an \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{instance }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{example }\DIFaddend being session \#2 in AHL of subject \#1). The Euclidean distance from the origin ($O$) was \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{subsequently }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{then }\DIFaddend calculated (Figure 1E).

\DIFdel{, median }%DIFDELCMD < [%%%
\DIFdel{IQR}%DIFDELCMD < ]%%%
\DIFdel{, }\textit{\DIFdel{n}} %DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{= 664, in Mismatch OUT task}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\addtocounter{footnote}{-1}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend 

\subsection{Visualization of hippocampal neural trajectory during SWR in two-dimensional spaces}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Given }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Based on }\DIFaddend our observations of \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the }\DIFaddend neural trajectory 'jump' during SWR (Figure 5), we visualized the three-dimensional trajectories of pre-, mid-, and post-SWR events during the encoding and retrieval phases (Figure 6)\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, the distance between which was dependent on memory-load (Figure 3). }%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \indent
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{We accomplished the visualizationin two-dimensional spaces by linearly aligning peri-SWR trajectories, positioning }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{. For this visualization, we positioned }\DIFaddend $\mathrm{g_{E}}$ at the origin (0, 0) and $\mathrm{g_{R}}$ at the coordinate ($\mathrm{\lVert g_{E}g_{R} \rVert}$, 0) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. These aligned trajectories were then rotated around the $\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}$ axis (= x-axis), ensuring conservation of distances from the origin $O$ and angles between $\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}$ in the original three-dimensional spaces in the two-dimensional spaces.
}%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \indent
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The scatter plot in these }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{in }\DIFaddend two-dimensional spaces \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{portrays the distinctive distributions of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{by linearly aligning }\DIFaddend peri-SWR trajectories\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{based on phases and task types. For instance, one can distinguish that $\mathrm{\lVert \text{mid-eSWR}^+ \rVert}$ is larger than $\mathrm{\lVert \text{pre-eSWR}^+ \rVert}$ (Figure 6B), consistent with our earlier findings (Figure 5)}\DIFdelend . 

\subsection{Fluctuating hippocampal neural trajectories between encoding and retrieval states}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Following this}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Subsequently}\DIFaddend , we inspected the trajectory \textit{directions} based on $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}$. Directions of SWRs were identified by the neural trajectory at $-250$ ms and $+250$ ms from their center (i.e., $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{eSWR^+}}$). \DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \indent
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{We }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{From this data, we }\DIFaddend computed the density of $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{eSWR}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}$, $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{rSWR}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}$, and $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{eSWR}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{rSWR}}$ (Figure 7A--D).
    \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\overrightarrow{\mathrm{rSWR^-}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}$ exhibited biphasic distributions.
}%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \indent
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{By comparing the distribution of $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{rSWR^+}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}$ (Figures 7A \& B) with those of $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{rSWR^-}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}$ (Figures 7C \& D), we calculated the contributions of SWR (Figures 7E \& F), which unveiled a shift in the direction of $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}$ (Figures 7E \& F; see }\textit{\DIFdel{red rectangles}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{).
}%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \indent
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Additionally, only in the Mismatch OUT task was $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{eSWR^+}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{rSWR^+}}$ less than that of $\overrightarrow{\mathrm{eSWR^-}} \cdot \overrightarrow{\mathrm{rSWR^-}}$ (baseline periods) (Figure 7F; see }\textit{\DIFdel{pink circles}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{); stated differently, eSWRs and rSWRs directed in the opposing direction exclusively in the Mismatch OUT task but not in the Match IN task (Figure 7E; see }\textit{\DIFdel{pink circles}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{).
}%DIFDELCMD < \label{sec:results}%%%
\DIFdelend \section{Discussion}
This study \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{posited }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{hypothesized }\DIFaddend that hippocampal neurons \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{demonstrate unique }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{express distinct }\DIFaddend representations, or trajectories, in low-dimensional spaces during a working memory (WM) task in humans, specifically during sharp-wave ripple (SWR) periods. Initially, we projected the multiunit spikes from medial temporal lobe regions during a Sternberg task onto three-dimensional spaces using Gaussian-process factor analysis (GPFA) (Figure~\ref{fig:01}D--E and Figure~\ref{fig:02}A) \cite{yu_gaussian-process_2009}. The trajectory distance \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{among }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{amongst }\DIFaddend WM phases ($\mathrm{\lVert g_{F}g_{E} \rVert}$, $\mathrm{\lVert g_{F}g_{M} \rVert}$, $\mathrm{\lVert g_{F}g_{R} \rVert}$, $\mathrm{\lVert g_{E}g_{M} \rVert}$, $\mathrm{\lVert g_{E}g_{R} \rVert}$, and $\mathrm{\lVert g_{M}g_{R} \rVert}$) was larger in the hippocampus than in the entorhinal cortex (EC) and amygdala (Figure~\ref{fig:02}E), \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{indicating more dynamic }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{suggesting increased }\DIFaddend neural activity in the hippocampus during the WM task. Moreover, the trajectory distance between the encoding and retrieval phases in the hippocampus ($\mathrm{\lVert g_{F}g_{E} \rVert}$) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{positively correlated }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{displayed a positive correlation }\DIFaddend with memory load (Figure~\ref{fig:03}C--D), \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{thereby marking it as a reflection of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{indicating that it reflects }\DIFaddend WM processing. The neural trajectory in the hippocampus also \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{exhibited }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{showed }\DIFaddend a transient increase during SWRs (Figure~\ref{fig:05}). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Lastly}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Finally}\DIFaddend , the hippocampal neural trajectory \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{fluctuated }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{alternated }\DIFaddend between encoding and retrieval states, transitioning from encoding to retrieval during SWR events (Figure~\ref{fig:07}). Overall, these findings \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{highlight }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{emphasize }\DIFaddend the role of hippocampal neural activity in a WM task in humans \cite{naber_reciprocal_2001,van_strien_anatomy_2009,strange_functional_2014}.

We \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{discovered that the neural trajectory's distance }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{found that the distance of the neural trajectory }\DIFaddend among the four phases was longer in the hippocampus compared to the EC and amygdala, even when adjusting for the distance from origin $O$ ($\mathrm{\lVert g_{F} \rVert}$, $\mathrm{\lVert g_{E} \rVert}$, $\mathrm{\lVert g_{M} \rVert}$, and $\mathrm{\lVert g_{R} \rVert}$) in those regions (Figure~\ref{fig:02}C--E). These findings \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{corroborate the role of the hippocampus in the WM task, which aligns with previous }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{align with existing }\DIFaddend reports of hippocampal persistent firing in the maintenance phase \cite{boran_persistent_2019} \cite{kaminski_persistently_2017} \cite{kornblith_persistent_2017} \cite{faraut_dataset_2018}\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. However}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, reinforcing the role of the hippocampus in the WM task. Notably}\DIFaddend , by applying GPFA to multiunit activity during a one-second \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{level resolution of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{resolution }\DIFaddend WM task, we \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{found that the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{observed that the neural trajectory in }\DIFaddend low dimensional space \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{neural trajectory }\DIFdelend exhibits a memory-load dependency between the encoding and retrieval phases, represented as $\mathrm{\lVert g_{E}g_{R} \rVert}$ (Figure~\ref{fig:03}). These results reaffirm the association between the hippocampus and WM processing \cite{oso_boran_2020}.

The reliability of our analysis, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{restricted }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{confined }\DIFaddend to presumed CA1 regions (Figure~\ref{fig:04}), is supported by several \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{contributing }\DIFdelend factors. This focused approach is grounded in consistent \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{observations }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{reports }\DIFaddend that SWRs are synchronous with spike bursts of interneurons and pyramidal neurons \cite{buzsaki_two-stage_1989} \cite{quyen_cell_2008} \cite{royer_control_2012} \cite{hajos_input-output_2013}, potentially within a 50 $\mu$m radius of the recording site \cite{schomburg_spiking_2012}. In this study, we \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{observed }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{noted }\DIFaddend an increase in SWR occurrences at 0--400 ms of the retrieval phase (Figure~\ref{fig:04}D), \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{aligning with prior }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{paralleling previous }\DIFaddend studies demonstrating increased SWR occurrences before spontaneous verbal recall \cite{norman_hippocampal_2019} \cite{norman_hippocampal_2021}. This finding not only corroborates \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{but broadens the observation }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{earlier observations, but also broadens them by extending }\DIFaddend to a triggered retrieval \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{condition}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{stage}\DIFaddend . Additionally, the log-normal distributions of SWR duration and ripple band peak amplitude observed in this study (Figure~\ref{fig:04}C & E) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{correlate }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{are consistent }\DIFaddend with the consensus in \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{this }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the }\DIFaddend field \cite{liu_consensus_2022}. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Hence}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Therefore}\DIFaddend , our approach of \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{confining }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{restricting }\DIFaddend recording sites to probable CA1 regions likely \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{improved the precision }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{enhanced the accuracy }\DIFaddend of SWR detection. It \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{should be noted that an }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is essential to mention that the }\DIFaddend increase in trajectory distance from origin $O$ during SWR (Figure~\ref{fig:05}) may \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{have been skewed to a greater extent }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{be slightly skewed }\DIFaddend due to the channel selection; however, this does not \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{dramatically }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{severely }\DIFaddend impact our primary findings.

Interestingly, trajectory directions in the retrieval phase \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{oscillated }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{alternated }\DIFaddend between encoding and retrieval states \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{both in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{in both }\DIFaddend baseline and SWR periods (Figure~\ref{fig:07}C \& D). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Furthermore, the balance of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Moreover, }\DIFaddend these fluctuations transitioned from encoding to retrieval states during SWR (Figure~\ref{fig:07}E \& F). These findings concur with previous \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{studies suggesting SWR'}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{working theories suggesting SWR’}\DIFaddend s role in memory recall \cite{norman_hippocampal_2019} \cite{norman_hippocampal_2021}. Our results add \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{another layer of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{to this }\DIFaddend understanding, specifying that SWRs occur when \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the }\DIFaddend hippocampal representation transitions from encoding to retrieval states. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Therefore}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Hence}\DIFaddend , our findings \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{offer new }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{provide novel }\DIFaddend insights into hippocampal representations: (i) neural fluctuations between encoding and retrieval states during a WM task and (ii) SWR as a mechanism \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{facilitating }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{enabling }\DIFaddend the transition from encoding to retrieval states \cite{buzsaki_hippocampal_2015}.

Additionally, our \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{research reveals }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{study uncovers }\DIFaddend WM-task-specific directions between encoding and retrieval SWRs (Figure~\ref{fig:07}E--F). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Particularly}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Notably}\DIFaddend , encoding SWR and retrieval SWR pointed in opposing directions not \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{during }\DIFaddend a Match IN but \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{during }\DIFaddend a Mismatch OUT task. These \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{results might }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{findings may }\DIFaddend align with the memory engram theory \cite{liu_optogenetic_2012}. Indeed, the Match In task \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{showed subjects a once-seen }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{presented subjects with a previously seen }\DIFaddend letter, while the Mismatch OUT task \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{presented a novel letter not introduced }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{introduced a new letter not shown }\DIFaddend in the encoding phase. These \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{outcomes }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{results }\DIFaddend suggest that SWR relates to \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the }\DIFdelend working cognitive processes in humans.

In conclusion, our study has demonstrated that hippocampal activity \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{fluctuates }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{oscillates }\DIFaddend between encoding and retrieval states during a WM task and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{undergoes a significant shift }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{shifts significantly }\DIFaddend from encoding to retrieval during SWR periods.

\label{sec:discussion}

        	\caption{\DIFdelbeginFL \textbf{\DIFdelFL{Local field potential (LFP), multiunit activity, and neural trajectory of the hippocampus during a modified Sternberg task}} %DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \textbf{\DIFaddFL{Local Field Potential (LFP), Multiunit Activity, and Neural Trajectory of the Hippocampus during a Modified Sternberg Task}} \DIFaddendFL \cite{li_functional_2023, borders_hippocampal_2022, dimakopoulos_information_2022}}
\smallskip
\\
\textbf{\textit{A.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Representative }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Shown here are representative }\DIFaddendFL wideband LFP traces from iEEG signals\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{recorded in }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{, recorded from }\DIFaddendFL the left hippocampal head \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{. These were attained }\DIFdelendFL while the subject performed a modified Sternberg working memory task\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{, consisting }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{. The task consisted }\DIFaddendFL of fixation (1 s, \textit{gray}), encoding (2 s, \textit{blue}), maintenance (3 s, \textit{green}), and retrieval (2 s, \textit{red}) \cite{li_functional_2023, borders_hippocampal_2022, dimakopoulos_information_2022}. \textbf{\textit{B.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{The corresponding }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Displayed are the associated }\DIFaddendFL ripple band LFP traces \cite{schomburg_spiking_2012, behrens_induction_2005, norimoto_hippocampal_2018}. \textbf{\textit{C.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{The }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{This is the }\DIFaddendFL raster plot of multiunit spikes\DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{, }\DIFaddendFL derived from the LFP traces \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{using }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{utilizing }\DIFaddendFL a spike sorting algorithm \cite{niediek_reliable_2016}. \textbf{\textit{D.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Neural trajectory}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{The neural trajectory, }\DIFaddendFL determined by GPFA\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{on the basis of }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{, is based on the }\DIFaddendFL spike counts per unit with 50-ms bins \cite{yu_gaussian-process_2009}. The \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{dot circles represent }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{dotted circles symbolize }\DIFaddendFL the geometric median coordinates for each phase. \textbf{\textit{E.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Trajectory distance from the }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{The trajectory distance from }\DIFaddendFL origin $O$ \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{. Please note that }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{is shown. Note, }\DIFaddendFL the \textit{purple} and \textit{yellow} rectangles \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{indicate }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{highlight }\DIFaddendFL the timings for SWR$^+$ candidates and SWR$^-$ candidates (controls for SWR$^+$), respectively \cite{van_vugt_hippocampal_2010, scoville_loss_1957, kay_hippocampal_2016, nader_memory_2003, wilson_reactivation_1994, nadasdy_replay_1999, lee_memory_2002}.
}

        	\label{fig:01}
        \end{figure*}

\textbf{\textit{A.}} The \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{figure illustrates the }\DIFaddendFL neural trajectory in the first \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{three-dimensional factors }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{three dimensions }\DIFaddendFL computed using \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{the Gaussian Process Factor Analysis (}\DIFaddendFL GPFA\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{is illustrated}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{)}\DIFaddendFL . \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Smaller dots represent the }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Each smaller dot represents }\DIFaddendFL coordinates of 50-ms neural trajectory bins, \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{while }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{whereas }\DIFaddendFL larger dots outlined in \textit{black} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{denote the }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{symbolize }\DIFaddendFL geometric medians \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{for subsequent }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{of consecutive }\DIFaddendFL phases in the Sternberg working memory task: fixation (\textit{gray}), encoding (\textit{blue}), maintenance (\textit{green}), and retrieval (\textit{red})\cite{yu_gaussian-process_2009}. \textbf{\textit{B.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{This figure demonstrates }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{The graph reveals }\DIFaddendFL the log-likelihood of GPFA models in \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{conjunction with }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{relation to }\DIFaddendFL the number of dimensions employed \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{to embed }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{for embedding }\DIFaddendFL multi-unit spikes in \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{medial temporal lobe (}\DIFaddendFL MTL\DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{) }\DIFaddendFL regions. \DIFdelFL{determined to be }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{identified as }\DIFaddendFL three, \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{ascertained through the use of }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{determined using }\DIFaddendFL the elbow method\cite{virtanen_scipy_2020}. \textbf{\textit{C.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{In this segment, }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{This portion \DIFdelFL{subsequent }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{final }\DIFaddendFL representation indicates inter-phase trajectory distances within the MTL regions\cite{liu_consensus_2022}.

*\textit{p} < 0.05, bootstrap test)\cite{buzsaki_hippocampal_2015}\cite{ego-stengel_disruption_2010}\cite{fernandez-ruiz_long-duration_2019}. \textbf{\textit{E.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{The Significant differences were observed }\DIFaddendFL (***\textit{p} < 0.001, \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{utilizing }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{using }\DIFaddendFL the Brunner--Munzel test)\cite{norman_hippocampal_2019}\cite{diba_forward_2007}\cite{liu_consensus_2022}.

}}

\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \textbf{\DIFaddFL{Transient Alterations in Neural Trajectory During SWR}}

\textbf{\textit{A.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Represents }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Indicates }\DIFaddendFL the \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{mean }\DIFaddendFL distance from the origin ($O$) of the peri-sharp-wave-ripple (SWR) trajectory\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{expressed as the mean }%DIFDELCMD < \textpm %%%
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{, which is accompanied by }\DIFaddendFL a 95\% confidence interval \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{, which }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{that }\DIFaddendFL may not be \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{visible owing }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{visually detectable due }\DIFaddendFL to its narrow range \cite{girardeau_selective_2009,norman_hippocampal_2019,buzsaki_hippocampal_2015}. \textbf{\textit{B.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Illustrates }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Depicts }\DIFaddendFL the distance from the origin ($O$) during the pre-, mid-, and post-SWR periods (*\textit{p} $<$ 0.05, **\textit{p} $<$ 0.01, ***\textit{p} $<$ 0.001; \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{according to }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{per }\DIFaddendFL the Brunner--Munzel test \cite{boran_persistent_2019}). \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Abbreviations detailed as}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Definitions included are}\DIFaddendFL : SWR, sharp-wave ripple events; eSWR, SWR occurring \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{in }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{during }\DIFaddendFL the encoding phase; rSWR, SWR \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{happening during }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{transpiring in }\DIFaddendFL the retrieval phase; SWR$^+$, \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{a }\DIFaddendFL SWR event; SWR$^-$, \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{the }\DIFaddendFL control events \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{for }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{paired with }\DIFaddendFL SWR$^+$; pre-, mid-, or post-SWR, the time intervals from $-800$ to $-250$ ms, from $-250$ to $+250$ ms, \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{or }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{and }\DIFaddendFL from $+250$ to $+800$ ms, \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{respectively, }\DIFaddendFL each relative to the SWR center.

        \begin{figure*}[ht]
            \pdfbookmark[2]{ID 06}{figure_id_06}
        	\centering
            \includegraphics[width=1\textwidth]{./src/figures/.png/Figure_ID_06.png}
        	\caption{\DIFdelbeginFL \textbf{\DIFdelFL{Visualization of Neural Trajectory During SWR in Two-Dimensional Space
}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \textbf{
\DIFaddFL{Visualizing Neural Trajectory During SWR in Two-Dimensional Space
}}
\DIFaddendFL \smallskip
\\
\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Featured are }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{The presented }\DIFaddendFL neural trajectories \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{within the hippocampus }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{pertain to hippocampal activity }\DIFaddendFL during Sharp-Wave Ripple (SWR) events, \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{represented }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{shown }\DIFaddendFL in \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{a }\DIFdelendFL two-dimensional space. \textbf{\textit{A.}} Trajectories \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{during }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{representative of }\DIFaddendFL pre- (\textit{gray}), mid- (\textit{yellow}), and post-SWR$^-$ (\textit{black}) phases of an SWR event~\cite{buzsaki_hippocampal_2015}. \textbf{\textit{B.}} \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Corresponding trajectories for }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Trajectories corresponding to }\DIFaddendFL SWR$^+$ scenarios \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{as opposed }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{in contrast }\DIFaddendFL to SWR$^-$~\cite{fernandez-ruiz_long-duration_2019}. The magnitude of $\lVert \mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}} \rVert$ \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{fluctuates }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{exhibits fluctuations }\DIFaddendFL within sessions~\cite{liu_consensus_2022}. The \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{projection }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{projecting }\DIFaddendFL protocol \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{went }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{is }\DIFaddendFL as follows: initially, $\mathrm{g_{E}}$ was \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{placed }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{situated }\DIFaddendFL at the origin $O$ (0,0), and $\mathrm{g_{R}}$ at ($\lVert \mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}} \rVert$, 0) via linear transformation~\cite{kim_corticalhippocampal_2022}. Subsequently, the point cloud was rotated around the $\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}$ axis (the x-axis) \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{for compatibility }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{to be compatible }\DIFaddendFL with a two-dimensional environment~\cite{yu_gaussian-process_2009}. \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Consequently}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{Thus}\DIFaddendFL , both the distances from $O$ and the angles with \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{respect to }\DIFdelendFL the $\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}$ axis \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{were kept intact }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{remained unaltered }\DIFaddendFL from their \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{original }\DIFdelendFL three-dimensional \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{arrangement}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{configuration}\DIFaddendFL ~\cite{mcinnes_umap_2018}. Abbreviations: SWR \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{denotes }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{represents }\DIFaddendFL Sharp-Wave Ripple events; eSWR \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{refers to }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{denotes }\DIFaddendFL SWR during the encoding phase; rSWR \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{indicates }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{signifies }\DIFaddendFL SWR during the retrieval phase; SWR$^+$ \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{represents }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{typifies }\DIFaddendFL an SWR event; SWR$^-$ \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{designates }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{signals }\DIFaddendFL the control events for SWR$^+$; pre-SWR, mid-SWR, or post-SWR \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{specify }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{refer to }\DIFaddendFL the time interval from $-800$ to $-250$ ms, from $-250$ to $+250$ ms, or from $+250$ to $+800$ ms from the center of the SWR\DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{, }\DIFaddendFL respectively~\cite{zhang_hippocampal_2022}.
}
% width=1\textwidth
        	\label{fig:06}
        \end{figure*}
        \clearpage
        \begin{figure*}[ht]
            \pdfbookmark[2]{ID 07}{figure_id_07}
        	\centering
            \includegraphics[width=0.5\textwidth]{./src/figures/.png/Figure_ID_07.png}
        	\caption{\DIFdelbeginFL \textbf{\DIFdelFL{Neural Trajectory Directions of SWR based on Encoding and Retrieval States
}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \textbf{
\DIFaddFL{Directionality of Neural Trajectories in SWR based on Encoding and Retrieval States
}}
\DIFaddendFL \smallskip
\\
\textbf{\textit{A--B}} \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{The }\DIFaddendFL Kernel Density Estimation (KDE) distribution of $\protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{eSWR^+}}} \cdot \protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{rSWR^+}}}$ (\textit{pink circles}), $\protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{eSWR^+}}} \cdot \protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}}$ (\textit{blue triangles}), and $\protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{rSWR^+}}} \cdot \protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}}$ (\textit{red rectangles}) in \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{the }\DIFaddendFL Match IN (\textit{A}) and Mismatch OUT tasks (\textit{B}) \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{are presented}\DIFaddendFL ~\cite{li_functional_2023}. \textbf{\textit{C--D}} The corresponding distributions \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{of }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{in these tasks are represented toggling }\DIFaddendFL $\mathrm{SWR^-}$ \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{replace those }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{in place }\DIFaddendFL of $\mathrm{SWR^+}$\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{in }\textit{\DIFdelFL{A--B}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelendFL ~\cite{dimakopoulos_information_2022}. \textbf{\textit{E--F}} The differences \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{in }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{between the }\DIFaddendFL distributions of $\mathrm{SWR^+}$ and $\mathrm{SWR^-}$ \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{, emphasizing }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{accentuate }\DIFaddendFL the SWR components (\textit{E} = \textit{C} $-$ \textit{A}; \textit{F} = \textit{B} $-$ \textit{D})\DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{. Notice }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{, with }\DIFaddendFL the biphasic distributions of $\protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{rSWR^-}}} \cdot \protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{g_{E}g_{R}}}}$ \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{, underscoring }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{emphasizing the }\DIFaddendFL neural fluctuations between encoding and retrieval states during the Sternberg task~\cite{borders_hippocampus_2022}. \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{Conversely}\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{On the other hand}\DIFaddendFL , \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{in }\DIFdelendFL the Mismatch OUT task \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{, }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{showed }\DIFaddendFL inverse directionality between $\protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{eSWR^+}}}$ and $\protect\overrightarrow{{\mathrm{rSWR^+}}}$ (\textit{pink circles}) \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{which }\DIFaddendFL was \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{identified, but }\DIFdelendFL not \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{observed }\DIFaddendFL in the Match IN task (\textbf{\textit{E--F}})~\cite{naber_reciprocal_2001,van_strien_anatomy_2009}. Lastly, \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{observed }\DIFaddendFL transitions from retrieval to encoding \DIFdelbeginFL \DIFdelFL{states were observed }\DIFdelendFL \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{state }\DIFaddendFL for the SWR components \DIFaddbeginFL \DIFaddFL{occurred }\DIFaddendFL in both Match IN and Mismatch OUT tasks (\textit{red rectangles} in \textit{E--F})~\cite{niediek_reliable_2016,schomburg_spiking_2012}.
}
% width=0.5\textwidth
        	\label{fig:07}
        \end{figure*}
